# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Alert Evaluation Cycle Overrun

## Your Task

Grafana logs warn 'alert evaluation took longer than expected'. Find the Go source files in grafana/grafana that (1) implement the alerting evaluation scheduler tick and (2) detect and log when an evaluation cycle overruns its time budget.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

42-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the research and created the answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

I've identified the Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement the alerting evaluation scheduler tick and detect evaluation cycle overruns:

### **Core Files:**

1. **pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/ticker/ticker.go** - Implements the ticker that emits evaluation ticks at regular intervals (baseInterval, default 10s)

2. **pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/schedule.go** - Implements the scheduler main loop:
   - `Run()`: Creates and runs the ticker
   - `schedulePeriodic()`: Main event loop receiving ticks
   - `processTick()`: Processes each tick and schedules rule evaluations
   - `runJobFn()`: **Detects overruns and logs warning** "Tick dropped because alert rule evaluation is too slow"

3. **pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/alert_rule.go** - Implements evaluation cycle overrun detection:
   - `Eval()`: **Key method** that detects overruns by attempting a non-blocking read from the evaluation channel before sending a new evaluation
   - `Run()`: The rule evaluation routine that processes evaluations

4. **pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/scheduler.go** - Defines the `EvaluationMissed` metric that tracks missed evaluations

### **How Overrun Detection Works:**

When a ticker tick arrives and the scheduler needs to evaluate a rule:
1. The scheduler calls `alertRule.Eval(evaluation)` 
2. The `Eval()` method does a non-blocking read from the evaluation channel
3. If an unprocessed evaluation is still there, it's captured as "dropped"
4. When dropped ≠ nil, the scheduler logs the warning and increments the `grafana_alerting_schedule_rule_evaluations_missed_total` metric

This mechanism detects when an evaluation takes longer than the ticker interval, indicating a

It emits time.Time values to the channel C at predictable times. The ticker is designed to queue up ticks rather than drop them, allowing downstream components to detect when they're falling behind.\\n\\n## Scheduler Main Loop (pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/schedule.go)\\nThe scheduler coordinates the evaluation flow:\\n\\n1. **schedule.Run()** (line 177): Initializes the ticker with the base interval and invokes schedulePeriodic().\\n\\n2. **schedule.schedulePeriodic()** (line 248): The main event loop that receives ticks from the ticker's C channel. Returns both `success` (true/false) and the `droppedMsg` (which could be nil or the unprocessed evaluation)\\n\\nWhen a dropped message is returned (not nil), it indicates that the alert rule's evaluation routine was still processing the previous evaluation when the next tick arrived. When overruns are detected, the scheduler logs a warning and increments the missed evaluations metric.\"\n}\n",
